# Excalidraw Data

## Text Elements
Very Long Baseline Interferometry ^PiOqYGgv

VLBI is a radio interferometry technique that uses multiple widely separated
telescopes (baselines of thousands of kilometers) to simulate a single, enormous telescope ^tqReyKGU

The key goal is to achieve
extremely high angular resolution,
proportional to the baseline length
divided by the observing wavelength
enabling detailed observations
of compact cosmic sources
like black holes and quasars. ^5TRUwWO6

unit vector
to radio source ^WRUv7Rt1

Precession
and
Nutation ^QgNqQha7

diurnal spin
(daily rotation of
earth around its axis) ^wIgcSGfV

Polar
motion ^Fh4MLMXJ

baseline vector
between two
stations ^a2vV4PnG

geometric delay
which describes the projection
of the baseline onto the direction
of the quasar to get the difference
in distance divided by speed of light
aka time diff accounting for all
EOP ^RU3EMlrz

determination of complete set of EOP ^aU6zb4fU

Each telescope records
incoming radio signals
(amplitude and phase)  ^5zuKOJ1n

nanosecond accuracy,
ensuring synchronization ^jRok4bMm

Telescopes' locations are tracked to millimeter precision using GPS and models of tectonic motion. ^eInw5xDn

Data from all stations are combined in a correlator, which adjusts for time delays caused by:

 1. Geometric baseline differences
(relative positions of telescopes).

 2. Earth’s rotation (continuously changing baseline orientation).

3. Atmospheric effects (ionospheric/tropospheric delays, corrected via models). ^UjTGNWMH

APPLICATIONS ^cocSMf03

The realization and maintenance
of the global reference frames (ICRF) ^bpgOntwh

Consistency with
higher radio frequencies ^wwVxZQx5

VLBI provides the precise length of intercontinental
baselines (up to 10.000 km and more), which strongly
support the realization and stability of the ITRF ^JQUCK18e

Detection of baseline
distance changes per 
year ^KK4mEyr7

models for Inferring
the movement
of plate tectonics ^8rCK2ocY

VLBI observes radio waves from quasars,
which are extragalactic and effectively stationary.
Any apparent motion in their positions
reflects changes in Earth’s orientation. ^3EgBHi01

By comparing observed delays meassured with VLBI
with theoretical predictions,
VLBI solves for polar motion (xp​, yp) which is the
deviation of earths pole from its crust, and UT1.
DUT1 is then derived as DUT1=UT1−UTClock.
DUT1 is the correction between earth real observed time
and the atomic clock time to not allow clocks to drift away
from reality. ^lQbcvqGE

Determination of precession +long-term nutation ^sv6qQCXz

Over decades, VLBI tracks tiny shifts in quasar positions
caused by Earth’s axis motion. These are decomposed into:
    Precession: Linear drift in celestial pole position.
    Nutation: Periodic deviations ^3qvP7Ois

Satellite Laser Ranging ^M1LwDoUb

Our goal is to observe the satellite orbit and
compare it with modelled (computed) orbit using integration
Residuals o-c are the basis for parameter estimation, such as
• orbital elements,
• gravity field spherical harmonic coefficients,
• ground station coordinates,
• tracking system quantification (biases, scales, etc.) ^bj3K9nZc

Measures the distance between ground
stations and satellites using laser pulses.
The time taken for the pulse to travel to the satellite
and back is used to calculate the distance  ^w7DZixuU

The accuracy of the ranging is dependent on 
the orbital height of the satellite
the time resolution of the electronics
the elimination of systematic errors
 ^BHKNoO2x

Satellite position
Integration of the equation of motion
but we dont know ^mmdxQeXl

Time
of
Flight ^0eU6z5kp

Atmospheric
(Ionosphere,
troposphere)
Correction ^8lCiPIbA

Corrects for
systematic errors
in the SLR system ^4B9UujG7

Station coordinates
(Earth fixed)
regularized station position and
instantaneous position ^yLCSv7Fc

Earth rotation ^ch9sLdd1

- Initial position and velocity
- Gravity field coefficients
- Drag coefficients
- Empirical parameters
(e.g. once per revolution) ^8CwNEszx

Correction for

Solid Earth tides
periodic deformation due to gravitational pull of the Moon/Sun

Ocean tidal loading
deformation from ocean mass redistribution

Ocean pole tides and Pole tides
deformation due to polar motion

Atmospheric pressure loading
deformation from atmospheric mass changes ^lWv62q0T

Regularized
station position
Represents a "smoothed" or
averaged position over time,
filtered to remove
short-term fluctuations. ^MMUbPNT5

V.S ^drznpP4U

Instantaneous
The station’s actual
position at a specific time t,
including all short-term deformations.
Calculated by adding
time-dependent corrections  ^aTssvICm

depends on Earth orientation
parameters (EOP) Every day ^13uil14L

satellite
geometric
correction ^KQe9qYD3

dd ^7SFJkDhm

station
geometric
correction ^nhUhYh8V

 signal calibration delay ^dSzP81au

Atmospheric
correction ^nHnJk4c4

Troposphere correction ^NKeEs0My

the height of the
atmosphere at which
the atmosphere
does not affect the
tracking signal ^9B49InnT

refractive index ^DcafV7gG

atmospheric
pressure and temp ^G8nJeFue

vapor
pressure ^P0y3u79l

relative humidity ^yfyXuaQS

How do retroreflectors reflect the laser? ^ezGQwAMC

SLR prisms are corner-cube retroreflectors that
have three mutually perpendicular reflective surfaces.
the laser reflects off each of the three surfaces in sequence.
The geometry ensures the outgoing light is directed back toward the source
regardless of the prism's orientation ^eyqm9aCm

triple prisms cover a narrower (Cut-off) angular range but maximize
signal strength over long distances for HEO ^zynZY37b

The strength of the signal is then proportional to
Signal strength decays with the fourth power of distance (double path)
the area of the satellite reflector
indirectly proportional to the square of the divergence angle
of the satellite reflector ^JpqMDo5b

Lunar laser ranging ^dwp6TCwa

Requires strong lasers to cover the large distance,
with a small return rate, high pointing accuracy and ~15m
prediction accuracy of the reflector position

Through LLR experiment we found out that:
The Moon is spiraling away from Earth at a rate of 3.8 cm per year
The Moon probably has a liquid core of about 20% of the Moon's radius.
The universal force of gravity is very stable ^CC57J47F

Precise Range and Range Rate Equipment ^NSS2g99b

Two-way two frequency microwave satellite
capable of measuring
highly accurate pn-coded ranges (= radial distances via code correlation) and carrier shifted range-rates
(= relative velocities via doppler shift) between space and ground at the same time and fully
synchronously.

Consists of Four independent, parallel, strictly coherently operating receiver channels,
which can track four PRARE ground stations that are in view of the satellite simultaneously.
And ultra-stable oscillator, temperature-controlled electronics in space
and
    29 gound stations with parabolic antennas and meteorological sensors.

 ^pwvvalsW

1.
The ground station transmits a
coded microwave signal (X/S-band)
to the satellite. ^0VxpT60A

2.
The satellite’s PRARE system
receives the signal, filters itm
decodes the data, transposes the frequency
to the uplink frequency and sends it back
with extra site-specific low-rate information
to the ground station. ^bq4ECiMT

3.
By correlating the transmitted
and received signals, PRARE
calculates the time delay
(for range) and frequency shift
(for range-rate).
(The ground station uses a GPS controlled
atomic clock for time) ^ONKdSneK

3.1
Delay Locked Loop:
Measures the time delay
between the transmitted
and received signals.


However this signal is period which
can create multiple matches, how do
we solve the ambiguity?
The BARKER code helps resolve
these ambiguities by providing a
unique timing reference every 1 second,
ensuring synchronization between
the satellite and ground station clocks. ^2lciGGDj

3.2
Phase Locked Loop:
Measures the Doppler shift
(frequency change) caused by relative motion
between the satellite and ground station.
(counting the cycles of the difference frequency)
which is then used to compute range-rate ^KWACVSfe

Range = 1/2​⋅c⋅Δt ^uobYqU8h

Range-rate = ​Δf⋅c/fcarrier​ ^Vdvo32Yl

This is done via
8bit BARKER code
which has autocorrelation properties
tominimize false matches ^T1stKxQJ

Doppler
shift ^a0gTIokH

Ultra Stable Oscillator ^ti7cCBWJ

The oscillator is designed for two purposes

1. Time Tagging:
Assigning precise timestamps to signal generation and communication processes.
Which ensures precise timing for individual measurements 

2. System Synchronization:
Maintaining synchronization across the entire PRARE system
Generates periodic synchronization pulses to align all ground station clocks.
Ensures measurements from different stations are time-aligned
which is critical for accurate data correlation. ^23kz1uqz

An advantage of this is that only the space segment oscillator has to
be monitored externally to assure the system's adequate timing. ^UzVPfD5M

DORIS
(Doppler Orbitography and Radiopositioning Integrated by Satellite) ^7p4iOevz

Time of closest
approach the frequency
of the received signal is equal
to the emitted one ^mASCHrD2

The satellite is moving closer
to the station thus the frequency
observed is greater than the
one emitted ^ureGuMFV

The satellite is moving farther
to the station thus the frequency
observed is lesser than the
one emitted ^WmwUJTeD

DORIS is one-way Doppler system where ground beacons emit dual-frequency signals
omni-directionally that are then observed by satellite at different locations in their orbits, and aids 
in the computation of the doppler shift of the satellite from the ground stations perspective.
Satellites then transmit that data to ground stations for further analysis and preprocessing ^E4tkJHdC

This is really useful in Orbit determination
By integrating the relative velocity over time, DORIS calculates the change
in distance between the satellite and the beacon. Which is usually used for
altimetry missions, analysis of satellite maneuvers and atmospheric drag
but can also be used for positioning help us produce time series data of the ground stations
movement with the tectonic plates and understanding pole coordinates over time ^laQOSnEi

Doppler Shift ^NE31e4oY
